قال : هكذا فلا سبيل إلى درك مطلوب مجهول إلا من قبل حاصل معلوم، ولا سبيل أيضاً إلى ذلك إلا بالتفطن للجهة التي لأجلها صار مؤدياً إلى المطلوب، فأشار بالتفطن للجهة المذكورة إلى تلك الملاحظة وهي من قبيل التصور دون التصديق فلا تسلسل ( وقد احتج البعض) يعني القاضي البيضاوي ) على رأي ابن سينا) وكون التفطن شرطاً للانتاج باختلاف الأشكال في الجلاء والخفاء) فإنا نجد شكلين يتركب كل منهما من مقدمتين بديهتين، مع أن إنتاج أحدهما لنتيجته بين جلي وإنتاج الآخر خفي، محتاج إلى بيان وما ذاك إلا لأن هيئة الأول قريبة من الطبع يتفطن لها بالبديهة وهيئة الثاني بعيدة منه فلا يتفطن لها إلا بدليل أو تنبيه ( وفيه نظر لاختلاف اللوازم ( في الأشكال ( فقد يكون إنتاجها لبعض ) من تلك اللوازم ( أظهر) من إنتاجها لبعض آخر منها، وتفصيل الكلام أن الأشكال مختلفة على سبيل منع الخلو إما في المقدمات وإما في النتائج فإذا فرض الاتحاد في المقدمتين في الأول والرابع كان اللازم من أحدهما عكس اللازم من الآخر، وإذا كان أحد الاختلافين لازماً، وقد يجتمعان أيضاً جاز أن يكون الاختلاف في الجلاء والخفاء لاختلاف اللوازم، أو لاختلاف الملزومات، أو لاختلافهما معاً، فإن اللزوم بين أمرين قد يكون بينا، ولا يكون بين أمرين آخرين، أو بين أحدهما وأمر آخر بيناً ( والحق أنه إن أراد ) ابن سينا بما ذكره وجعله شرطاً للانتاج ( اجتماع المقدمتين معاً في الذهن) مرتبتين على ما ينبغي (فمسلم) لأنه لو كان حصول المبادي وحدها بلا ترتيب معتبر بينها، كافياً في حصول المطلوب لكان العالم بالقضايا الواجب قبولها عالماً بجميع المبادئ هيئة مخصوصة عارضة لها هي صورة للنظر كما مر ( وإن أراد أمراً) آخر ) وراءه ) أي وراء الاجتماع المذكور (فممنوع) إذ لا حاجة بنا بعد ترتيب المقدمتين على هيئة الشكل الأول إلى أمر آخر، والحاصل أنه لا بد مع المقدمتين من الترتيب والهيئة ومن أن تكون لهما نسبة مخصوصة مع النتيجة، وأما ملاحظة الترتيب والهيئة والنسبة المخصوصة فلا دليل على كونها شرطاً سوى قضية جلاء الأشكال وخفائها وقد عرفت ما فيها ( وما ذكره من المثال ( في البلغة (إنما يصح عند الذهول عن إحدى المقدمتين وأما عند ملاحظتهما على الترتيب اللائق ( فلا ) ذلك المثال، نعم إذا لوحظ الكبرى قبل الصغرى كان الترتيب مفقوداً، وأمكن ذلك الظن . قوله: (فممنوع) قد عرفت مما حررنا لك سقوط هذا المنع. قوله: (وأما ملاحظة الترتيب إلخ) وقد عرفت أنه عبارة عن ملاحظة اندراج الأصغر بخصوصه تحت الأوسط وأنه لا شبهة في كونه شرطاً، فلا يلزم من عدم كون ملاحظة الترتيب شرطاً عدم كون ملاحظة الاندراج شرطاً ، نعم إنه يصح رداً على ما قاله القاضي البيضاوي .
He said: Thus there is no way to apprehend an unknown sought object except from a known attained [premise], and there is also no way to that except by awareness (التفطن) of the aspect (الجهة) for which it became leading to the sought object. So he indicated by 'awareness of the mentioned aspect' to that observation (الملاحظة), and it is of the type of conceptualization (التصور) not assent (التصديق), so there is no regress. (And some argued, meaning al-Qadi al-Baydawi, against the opinion of Ibn Sina, that awareness is a condition for production (الإنتاج) due to the difference of the figures (الأشكال) in clarity and obscurity. For we find two figures each composed of two evident premises, while the production of one for its conclusion is clear and evident and the production of the other is obscure, needing explanation. That is only because the form (الهيئة) of the first is close to nature, so one is aware of it by intuition (البديهة), and the form of the second is far from it, so one is not aware of it except by a proof or alert. (And there is a consideration due to the difference of the implications (اللوازم) in the figures. For their production of some of those implications may be more apparent than their production of some others. The detailed speech is that the figures differ, by way of mutual exclusion, either in the premises or in the conclusions. So if identity is assumed in the two premises in the first and fourth, the implication (اللازم) from one is the converse of the implication from the other. And if one of the two differences is necessary, and they may also both combine, it is possible that the difference in clarity and obscurity is due to the difference of the implications, or the difference of the implied things, or the difference of both together. For the implication (اللزوم) between two things may be evident, and not evident between two other things, or between one and another thing is evident. (And the truth is that if Ibn Sina intended by what he mentioned and made it a condition for production (the conjunction of the two premises together in the mind) arranged as they ought to be, then it is accepted. Because if obtaining the principles alone without a considered order between them were sufficient for obtaining the sought, then the knower of the propositions that must be accepted would know... with all the principles a particular form accidental to them which is the form of reasoning as earlier. And if he intended something else beyond it, i.e., beyond the mentioned conjunction, then it is denied, for we have no need after arranging the two premises in the form of the first figure for another thing. The summary is that with the two premises, arrangement and form are necessary, and that they have a particular relation with the conclusion. As for observing the arrangement, form, and particular relation, there is no proof for it being a condition other than the issue of the clarity and obscurity of the figures, and you have known what is in it. (And what he mentioned of the example in al-Bulgha, it is only valid when one is heedless of one of the two premises. As for when they are observed in the proper order, that example is not valid. Yes, if the major is observed before the minor, the arrangement is missing, and that opinion is possible. His statement: ('Denied') - You have known from what we have written for you the fall of this denial. His statement: ('And as for observing the arrangement, etc.') - And you have known that it is an expression of observing the inclusion (اندراج) of the minor in particular under the middle, and that there is no doubt of it being a condition. So it does not follow from the fact that observing the arrangement is not a condition that observing the inclusion is not a condition. Indeed, it is valid as a refutation of what al-Qadi al-Baydawi said.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage begins by defining the condition of awareness (التفطن) for reasoning (النظر) to yield knowledge. The author states that a sought unknown can only be reached from a known premise, and only through awareness of the aspect that makes the premise lead to the sought. This awareness is a conceptualization (تصور), not an assent (تصديق), so there is no regress. Then an objection by al-Qadi al-Baydawi against Ibn Sina's view is presented: the difference in clarity and obscurity among the logical figures proves that awareness of the form is a condition, since two figures composed of equally evident premises can produce one clear and one obscure conclusion. The author critiques this objection: the difference in clarity may be due to differences in implications (اللوازم) or implied things (الملزومات), not necessarily to awareness of the form. The discussion analyzes the nature of implication between two things and how it can vary. The author then states the correct position: if Ibn Sina meant the conjunction of the two premises in the mind arranged properly, it is accepted; if he meant something beyond that, it is denied. There is no need for an additional act beyond the proper arrangement. The example from al-Bulgha is valid only when one is heedless of one premise; otherwise, it is not. Finally, the commentator clarifies that observing the inclusion of the minor under the middle is indeed a condition, and this refutes al-Qadi al-Baydawi.

Correction: The passage argues that awareness (التفطن) of the logical form is necessary; simply possessing premises is not enough. The mind must recognize how the premises lead to the conclusion.

D) Because the condition is only for obscure figures.

Key Takeaway
Reasoning requires not just premises but also awareness of how they are arranged and of the inclusion of the minor under the middle, which is the key to producing knowledge.

Knowledge of Indication vs. Knowledge of the Indicated
Al-Razi's three-part distinction and the ensuing dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between knowledge of a proof's indication and knowledge of its conclusion, and the reasons for the scholarly dispute on this issue.

Core Idea
The indication of a proof is a distinct relation, not identical to the proof or the conclusion.

This lesson examines a key question in Islamic logic and theology: Is knowing how a proof points to its conclusion the same as knowing the conclusion itself? Imam al-Razi and others drew a careful distinction, while some disagreed. The passage below lays out the main positions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage slowly. Then read the translation. Notice the three distinct entities al-Razi identifies: proof, indication, and indicated.
The passage uses technical terms like دليل, مدلول, and دلالة.
2
Identify al-Razi's argument
Al-Razi argues that the proof and the indicated are distinct, and the indication is a relation between them, also distinct. Therefore the knowledges of these are distinct. Confirm this reasoning from the text.
3
Contrast the other views
Another group adds that the aspect of indication (وجه الدلالة) is separate from the proof, while others deny any such distinction. Notice how the commentator refutes the denial.
Aspect of indication example: the world's temporality or contingency.
4
Reflect on the significance
Consider why this distinction matters for theology: it affects how we understand the process of reasoning from creation to Creator.
This is foundational for arguments like the kalam cosmological argument.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المقصد العاشر : هل يغاير العلم بالمدلول ] قد اختلف في أن العلم بدلالة الدليل على المدلول (هل يغاير العلم بالمدلول قال الإمام الرازي: هناك دليل (مستلزم كوجود العالم ( ومدلول (لازم) كوجود الصانع ( ودلالة هي نسبة بينهما متأخرة عنهما ولا شك أنها متغايرة، فتكون العلوم المتعلقة بها متغايرة أيضاً ( ثم قال قوم: وجه الدلالة غير الدليل كما نقول العالم يدل على وجود الصانع لحدوثه أو إمكانه ) فالدليل هو العالم ووجه دلالته ) هو ( الحدوث ) أو الإمكان ) وهو مغاير له عارض وقال آخرون : لا يجب ذلك ) أي قوله: (فممنوع) قد عرفت مما حررنا لك سقوط هذا المنع. قوله: (وأما ملاحظة الترتيب إلخ) وقد عرفت أنه عبارة عن ملاحظة اندراج الأصغر بخصوصه تحت الأوسط وأنه لا شبهة في كونه شرطاً، فلا يلزم من عدم كون ملاحظة الترتيب شرطاً عدم كون ملاحظة الاندراج شرطاً ، نعم إنه يصح رداً على ما قاله القاضي البيضاوي . مع قوله : (قد اختلف إلخ) وجه الاختلاف في مغايرة العلم بالدلالة للعلم بالمدلول غير ظاهر، أن الدليل الذي ذكره الإمام يفيد مغايرته للعلم بالدليل والعلم بالمدلول، إفادة لا يخفى على من له أدنى تمييز وكذا لا اشتباه في مغايرة وجه الدلالة، أي الأمر الذي بواسطته ينقل الذهن من الدليل إلى المدلول للدليل فإن تعريفه ينادي على مغايرته فكيف خفي على الفحول وكيف اختلفوا فيه. قوله : (إذ لا حاجة بنا إلخ ) فإن قلت المتناهي في البلادة ربما يرتب المقدمتين على هيئة الشكل الأول، ومع ذلك تخفى عليه النتيجة ويغفل عن لزومها بسبب غفلته عن أن الأصغر يندرج تحت الأوسط، قلت : الظاهر أن الغفلة بسبب عدم قدرته على جمع المقدمتين .
The Tenth Objective: Whether the knowledge of the indicated (المدلول) differs [from knowledge of the indication]. It has been disputed whether the knowledge of the indication (الدلالة) of the proof (الدليل) upon the indicated differs from the knowledge of the indicated. Imam al-Razi said: There is a proof (دليل) (implicant, like the existence of the world), and an indicated (مدلول) (implicate, like the existence of the Creator), and an indication (دلالة) which is a relation between them posterior to them, and there is no doubt that they are distinct. So the knowledges pertaining to them are also distinct. Then a group said: The aspect of indication (وجه الدلالة) is other than the proof, as we say 'the world indicates the existence of the Creator due to its temporal origination (حداثة) or its contingency (إمكان).' So the proof is the world, and its aspect of indication is temporality or contingency, and it is other than it, accidental. And others said: That is not necessary. His statement: ('Denied') - You have known from what we have written for you the fall of this denial. His statement: ('And as for observing the arrangement, etc.') - And you have known that it is an expression of observing the inclusion (اندراج) of the minor under the middle, and that there is no doubt of it being a condition. So it does not follow from the fact that observing the arrangement is not a condition that observing the inclusion is not a condition. Indeed, it is valid as a refutation of what al-Qadi al-Baydawi said. With his statement: ('It has been disputed, etc.') - The reason for the dispute on the distinctness of the knowledge of the indication from the knowledge of the indicated is not apparent, for the proof that the Imam mentioned indicates its distinctness from the knowledge of the proof and the knowledge of the indicated, an indication not hidden from anyone with the least discrimination. Likewise, there is no confusion in the distinctness of the aspect of indication, i.e., the matter by which the mind is transferred from the proof to the indicated; for its definition proclaims its distinctness. So how was it hidden from the great scholars and how did they dispute it? His statement: ('For we have no need, etc.') - If you say: The extremely dull person might arrange the two premises in the form of the first figure, yet the conclusion remains hidden from him and he is heedless of its implication due to his heedlessness that the minor is included under the middle. I say: It appears that the heedlessness is due to his inability to combine the two premises.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage opens the tenth objective: whether knowledge of the indication of a proof is distinct from knowledge of the indicated conclusion. The author presents Imam al-Razi's view: there are three distinct things—proof, indicated, and the indication (relation) between them. Since these are distinct, the knowledges of them are also distinct. Another group adds that the aspect of indication (وجه الدلالة), such as the world's temporality or contingency, is separate from the proof itself. Others disagree, denying this distinction. The commentator then notes that the reason for dispute on this matter is unclear because al-Razi's argument seems conclusive. The commentator also responds to a potential objection: a dull person may arrange premises correctly yet miss the conclusion due to heedlessness of the inclusion of the minor under the middle; the explanation is that this heedlessness stems from an inability to combine the two premises mentally, not from a lack of a separate knowledge of indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that the indication is identical to the proof or its aspect, but the passage shows they are separate cognitive objects.
Correction: The indication is a distinct relation, and the aspect of indication (e.g., temporality) is an attribute of the proof, not the proof itself.

Checkpoint
According to Imam al-Razi in the passage, what is the indication (الدلالة)?
A) The proof itself
B) The indicated conclusion
C) A relation between the proof and the indicated
D) The aspect of temporality

Key Takeaway
The knowledge of a proof's indication is distinct from the knowledge of its conclusion because the indication is a separate relation between them.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you affirm your belief in the Creator, do you rely on a mere echo of arguments heard from others, or have you personally traced the indication from the world to its Maker, distinguishing the proof from the relation? If you have not made this distinction, is your knowledge truly your own?
?
This lesson teaches that the aspect of indication (e.g., temporality) is a separate reality from the world itself. In your own life, do you look at the world and immediately see the hand of Allah, or do you pause to recognize the specific attribute that signals His existence? Your certainty depends on this pause—will you take it today?
?
Al-Razi insists that knowledge of the indication is distinct from knowledge of the conclusion. Have you ever treated the evidence for Allah as identical to the conclusion itself, perhaps reducing your faith to a mere assent? What would it take for you to properly separate the two and strengthen the foundation of your belief?

The Infinite Regress Argument for a Distinct Face of Indication
Presents the infinite regress argument and its critique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical argument that if the face of indication must materially differ from the evidence, it leads to infinite regress, and how this regress can be avoided.

Core Idea
Infinite regress only follows if the face itself is an evidence.

This lesson opens the discussion on whether the face of indication must differ from the evidence. The author presents a conditional argument: if a thing does not indicate by its essence, then every evidence needs a separate face, leading to infinite regress. However, the critique shows that the regress can be avoided if the face is not itself an evidence. We will follow this reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two key claims
The passage first states the necessity of a distinct face if indication is not by essence, leading to infinite regress. Then it critiques that claim. Read carefully to separate these two parts.
2
Understand the example of 'possibility'
The author uses the example of possibility (al-imkan) as a face of indication that itself becomes an evidence for the Maker. Consider why this is problematic and how the critique responds.
Possibility is a conceptual (اعتباري) matter.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The critique concludes that infinite regress only follows if the face of indication is also an evidence, which can be denied. So the obligation of a distinct face is not absolute.

The Fifth Observation - The Tenth Objective: Does knowledge of the signified differ. The face of indication being different from the evidence. (But a thing may indicate something else by considering its essence; otherwise) meaning if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence but it is necessary that every evidence has a face of indication that differs from it, then infinite regress would follow. Because we transfer the discussion to that face which is the cause of the evidence's indication, like possibility (al-imkan) for example, for it is also an evidence indicating the existence of the Maker, so it must have a face of indication that differs from it. (And temporal origination (al-huduth)) which is the face of indication is not other than the world which is the evidence. His statement: (It is not necessary, etc.) This and his statement: But a thing may indicate etc. are explicit that these people claimed the removal of obligation. His statement: (For it is also an evidence, etc.) has a discussion because if it is based on possibility being part of the world, then it would be evidence for the existence of the Maker, but it is objected that we do not accept that because it is a conceptual matter; and this indicates that what is evidence for the existence of the Maker must have its face of indication assuming difference as an evidence, and infinite regress only follows if the face of indication of every evidence is an evidence. It is permissible to end at an evidence whose face of indication is not an evidence for anything. And if it is based on the idea that since the evidence is evidence by virtue of that face, the face is in reality an evidence, it is denied because evidence is that through which one can reach correct consideration in it or its states, and consideration does not occur in its face of indication. His statement: (And others said: It is not necessary; rather a thing may indicate, etc.) For if you say: The apparent meaning of these two statements indicates the permissibility of difference in some attributes, and the latter part of the statement from its being based on what the mashayikh said indicates the non-permissibility of difference; I say: Even if the claim of actual basis is granted, we do not accept that it indicates the non-permissibility of difference absolutely. For the mashayikh, may Allah have mercy on them, do not claim for every attribute of a thing that it is neither it nor other. Rather, the attribute according to them may differ from its possessor if it is separable from its possessor, and may not differ if it is concomitant and inseparable, as the commentator will quote from al-Amidi in the sixth objective of the fourth observation on unity, multiplicity, and relation in his statement: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, by convention, and the intended meaning is the necessary attribute. So mere building upon what the mashayikh mentioned and the statement that the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence does not necessitate non-difference, for the face of indication may be an attribute of the evidence separable from it, like temporal origination (al-huduth) meaning coming out of non-existence into existence on the assumption of its existence, for it is something other than the contingent, as you will come to know in the second objective of the fourth observation on existence-based attributes; and it may not be separable from it, like possibility (al-imkan). And know that the seventh group claimed that the face of indication, e.g., temporal origination, is other than the evidence, i.e., the world absolutely. So the statement of the second group who deny obligation, 'Rather a thing may indicate' is an indication of a concessive argument for the negation of obligation, etc., i.e., if it is granted that temporal origination is other than the world, then the indication may be through temporal origination itself, so then there is no difference between the face of indication and the evidence, hence no obligation. And their statement that temporal origination is not other than the world is a prohibitive argument. Yes, if this had been presented earlier it would have been more appropriate. Thus, according to this direction, the preceding and following speech are connected, so ponder. A separable attribute. His statement: (It is not other than the world, based on what the statement of the first group indicates who claim the difference of temporal origination. An intermediary between the world, which is what is other than Allah (and the Maker); rather, everything that is other than Him is included in what is besides Him. So there is no third thing that is other than the world and the Maker, and we argue from the world to the Maker. (So there is no third thing that is other than the evidence and the signified. And this which these people mentioned is close to what our mashayikh said: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, as will come; rather it resembles being a branch of that, for the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, and you will come to know it) i.e., the state of the attribute in relation to its possessor. A critic said: al-Muhassal (the summary) of this question only occurs among the mutakallimun when they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, saying: Our mashayikh do not... His statement: (The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other) i.e., some attributes, namely the necessary ones, as will come by way of quote from al-Ash'ari that attributes include what is identical to the essence, like existence; and what is other than it, which is every attribute that can separate from its possessor, like attributes of action: His being Creator, Provider, and the like; and what is said to be neither identical nor other, which is what cannot separate from it in any way, like knowledge and power. So it does not respond to what is imagined that this requires that the statement of these people be absolute negation, while they explicitly state the removal of absolute obligation. His statement: For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, i.e., it may be an attribute of the evidence, so it does not contradict what preceded from him regarding what he stated that a thing may indicate by considering its essence and that temporal origination is not other than the world. His statement: (A critic said: al-Muhassal of this question, etc.) Since the origin that the author mentioned is extremely remote, he transmitted an origin for this disagreement that natures accept in general. His statement: (When they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, as they argue from existing contingent things to the Necessary, similarly they argue from the existence of contingent things to the existence of the Necessary, either by their possibility or by their being preceded by non-existence, so the speech is apparent and there is no need for interpretation, as imagined... of the world, and some went to the existentiality of temporal origination, although it is weak, otherwise it would not be included in the world which is what is other than Allah, for the world is the sum of existents, and non-existents are not described as difference terminologically, so they are absolutely not included in the world. His statement: (Rather it resembles being a branch, etc.) He only said 'resembles' because what just passed of their making temporal origination part of the world is not consistent with it; and although this can be interpreted as a concessive proof, their statement of identity in some places also does not suit it; and if by identity is meant only the negation of otherness, it would not apply to what is argued by negating temporal origination, for example. For these reasons he judged it as resemblance and did not definitively state it as branch. His statement: (For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence) i.e., in what is imagined to involve difference, like the argument from the world to the Maker, so it is not objected that this contradicts what that speaker explicitly stated: that the evidence may indicate something by considering its essence, otherwise infinite regress would follow.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on whether the face of indication (وجه الدلالة) must be different from the evidence (الدليل) itself. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical: if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence, then every evidence must have a face of indication that is distinct, leading to infinite regress (التسلسل). The example given is possibility (الإمكان) as a face for the evidence of the world's dependence on a Maker. However, the commentator then critiques this, noting that possibility is a conceptual (اعتباري) matter and that infinite regress only follows if every face is itself an evidence—which can be avoided if one stops at a face that is not evidence. Next, he discusses a second group who say it is not necessary for the face to differ; rather, a thing may indicate by its very essence. He reconciles this with the mashayikh's (المشايخ) principle that an attribute of a thing is neither the thing itself nor entirely other (صفة الشيء لا هو ولا غيره). The commentator explains that this principle does not universally negate difference; some attributes are separable (منفكة) like temporal origination (الحدوث) in the sense of coming from non-existence, while others are inseparable (لازمة) like possibility. The seventh group is introduced, claiming that the face (e.g., huduth) is absolutely other than the evidence (the world). The commentator then shows how the second group's argument, when concessively accepted, actually proves non-difference. The discussion continues with the assertion that there is no third entity between the world and the Maker; everything other than God is the world. This aligns with the mashayikh's view that the face is an attribute of the evidence. A critic (ناقد المحصل) is quoted suggesting that the whole dispute arises from how mutakallimun argue from the existence of contingent things to God, either through possibility or through being preceded by non-existence. Finally, clarification is given that the face of indication being an attribute of the evidence does not conflict with the possibility of indicating by essence, as long as the attribute is not considered separate in that context. The entire passage is a sophisticated logical analysis of the relationship between evidence, face of indication, and infinite regress, emphasizing the flexibility of the mashayikh's principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The face of indication must always be a distinct entity from the evidence, otherwise infinite regress follows.
Correction: Infinite regress only follows if the face itself is an evidence; it can be avoided if the face is not an evidence.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does infinite regress not necessarily follow from the requirement that every evidence has a distinct face of indication?
A) Because the face of indication can be identical to the evidence.
B) Because the face of indication may not itself be an evidence.
C) Because infinite regress is impossible in logical arguments.
D) Because the face of indication is always a conceptual matter.

Key Takeaway
The requirement that the face of indication differ from the evidence does not necessarily lead to infinite regress, because the face may not itself be an evidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the evidence for God's existence, do you find yourself demanding endless proofs, or can you accept a single clear evidence as sufficient to compel your faith? Which pattern characterizes your current spiritual state?
?
The passage shows that an evidence's face of indication may not itself be an evidence. Is there a point in your own search for truth where you have stopped asking 'what is the evidence for that evidence?' and instead allowed the original sign to settle your heart? If not, what is holding you back?
?
This lesson critiques the assumption that every evidence needs a distinct face. In your life, have you ever treated a clear sign from God as insufficient, demanding further proof? How might this lesson free you to trust the direct indication of creation rather than multiply intermediaries?

The Second Group and the Mashayikh's Principle on the Face of Indication
Discusses the second group's view and reconciles it with the mashayikh's principle.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the mashayikh's principle that 'the attribute of a thing is neither it nor other' applies to the face of indication, allowing for both identity and difference depending on whether the attribute is separable or inseparable.

Core Idea
The face of indication can be either identical or different, depending on the attribute's separability.

After the initial argument, a second group claims that it is not necessary for the face of indication to differ from the evidence. This raises the question of the mashayikh's principle. In this lesson, we explore how the mashayikh's rule is nuanced, distinguishing between inseparable and separable attributes, and how this applies to the face of indication.

Guided Path
1
Identify the second group's claim
Read the passage to find the statement that it is not necessary for the face to differ; the evidence may indicate by its essence.
2
Understand the challenge based on the mashayikh's principle
The apparent meaning of the second group's statement seems to conflict with the mashayikh's principle. See how the commentator resolves this.
3
Learn the distinction between separable and inseparable attributes
The commentator explains that the mashayikh's principle only applies to necessary (لازمة) attributes. Attributes that can separate (منفكة) may be different. See examples: temporal origination (separable) and possibility (inseparable).

فلا يرد ما يتوهم من أن هذا يقتضي أن يكون قول هؤلاء السلب الكلي مع أنهم مصرحون برفع الإيجاب الكلي . قوله : فإن وجه الدلالة صفة للدليل أي قد يكون صفة الدليل فلا ينافي ما تقدم منه من ( أنه قد يدل الشيء بوجود ما سوى الله على وجوده (تعالى كما يستدلون بالممكنات الموجودة على الواجب ،تعالى كذلك يستدلون بوجود الممكنات على وجود الواجب، إما بإمكانه أو بمسبوقيته بالعدم فالكلام على ظاهره ولا حاجة إلى التأويل على ما وهم ، للعالم، وذهب إليه البعض من وجودية الحدوث وإن كان مزيفاً، وإلا لا يكون داخلاً في العالم الذي هو ما سوى الله تعالى، إذ العالم هو جملة الموجودات وأما المعدومات فلا توصف بالمغايرة اصطلاحاً، بعض المواضع لا يلائمه أيضا ولو أريد بالعينية سلب الغيرية فقط، لم يتجه فيما استدل بنفي الحدوث مثلاً ، ولهذه المعاني حكم بالشبه ولم يقطع بالفرعية . قوله : ( فإن وجه الدلالة صفة للدليل أي فيما يتوهم فيه المغايرة كالاستدلال بالعالم على الصانع ،تعالى فلا يرد أن هذا مخالف لما صرح به ذلك القائل من أن الدليل قد يدل على الشيء نظراً إلى ذاته وإلا لزم التسلسل
The Fifth Observation - The Tenth Objective: Does knowledge of the signified differ. The face of indication being different from the evidence. (But a thing may indicate something else by considering its essence; otherwise) meaning if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence but it is necessary that every evidence has a face of indication that differs from it, then infinite regress would follow. Because we transfer the discussion to that face which is the cause of the evidence's indication, like possibility (al-imkan) for example, for it is also an evidence indicating the existence of the Maker, so it must have a face of indication that differs from it. (And temporal origination (al-huduth)) which is the face of indication is not other than the world which is the evidence. His statement: (It is not necessary, etc.) This and his statement: But a thing may indicate etc. are explicit that these people claimed the removal of obligation. His statement: (For it is also an evidence, etc.) has a discussion because if it is based on possibility being part of the world, then it would be evidence for the existence of the Maker, but it is objected that we do not accept that because it is a conceptual matter; and this indicates that what is evidence for the existence of the Maker must have its face of indication assuming difference as an evidence, and infinite regress only follows if the face of indication of every evidence is an evidence. It is permissible to end at an evidence whose face of indication is not an evidence for anything. And if it is based on the idea that since the evidence is evidence by virtue of that face, the face is in reality an evidence, it is denied because evidence is that through which one can reach correct consideration in it or its states, and consideration does not occur in its face of indication. His statement: (And others said: It is not necessary; rather a thing may indicate, etc.) For if you say: The apparent meaning of these two statements indicates the permissibility of difference in some attributes, and the latter part of the statement from its being based on what the mashayikh said indicates the non-permissibility of difference; I say: Even if the claim of actual basis is granted, we do not accept that it indicates the non-permissibility of difference absolutely. For the mashayikh, may Allah have mercy on them, do not claim for every attribute of a thing that it is neither it nor other. Rather, the attribute according to them may differ from its possessor if it is separable from its possessor, and may not differ if it is concomitant and inseparable, as the commentator will quote from al-Amidi in the sixth objective of the fourth observation on unity, multiplicity, and relation in his statement: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, by convention, and the intended meaning is the necessary attribute. So mere building upon what the mashayikh mentioned and the statement that the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence does not necessitate non-difference, for the face of indication may be an attribute of the evidence separable from it, like temporal origination (al-huduth) meaning coming out of non-existence into existence on the assumption of its existence, for it is something other than the contingent, as you will come to know in the second objective of the fourth observation on existence-based attributes; and it may not be separable from it, like possibility (al-imkan). And know that the seventh group claimed that the face of indication, e.g., temporal origination, is other than the evidence, i.e., the world absolutely. So the statement of the second group who deny obligation, 'Rather a thing may indicate' is an indication of a concessive argument for the negation of obligation, etc., i.e., if it is granted that temporal origination is other than the world, then the indication may be through temporal origination itself, so then there is no difference between the face of indication and the evidence, hence no obligation. And their statement that temporal origination is not other than the world is a prohibitive argument. Yes, if this had been presented earlier it would have been more appropriate. Thus, according to this direction, the preceding and following speech are connected, so ponder. A separable attribute. His statement: (It is not other than the world, based on what the statement of the first group indicates who claim the difference of temporal origination. An intermediary between the world, which is what is other than Allah (and the Maker); rather, everything that is other than Him is included in what is besides Him. So there is no third thing that is other than the world and the Maker, and we argue from the world to the Maker. (So there is no third thing that is other than the evidence and the signified. And this which these people mentioned is close to what our mashayikh said: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, as will come; rather it resembles being a branch of that, for the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, and you will come to know it) i.e., the state of the attribute in relation to its possessor. A critic said: al-Muhassal (the summary) of this question only occurs among the mutakallimun when they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, saying: Our mashayikh do not... His statement: (The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other) i.e., some attributes, namely the necessary ones, as will come by way of quote from al-Ash'ari that attributes include what is identical to the essence, like existence; and what is other than it, which is every attribute that can separate from its possessor, like attributes of action: His being Creator, Provider, and the like; and what is said to be neither identical nor other, which is what cannot separate from it in any way, like knowledge and power. So it does not respond to what is imagined that this requires that the statement of these people be absolute negation, while they explicitly state the removal of absolute obligation. His statement: For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, i.e., it may be an attribute of the evidence, so it does not contradict what preceded from him regarding what he stated that a thing may indicate by considering its essence and that temporal origination is not other than the world. His statement: (A critic said: al-Muhassal of this question, etc.) Since the origin that the author mentioned is extremely remote, he transmitted an origin for this disagreement that natures accept in general. His statement: (When they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, as they argue from existing contingent things to the Necessary, similarly they argue from the existence of contingent things to the existence of the Necessary, either by their possibility or by their being preceded by non-existence, so the speech is apparent and there is no need for interpretation, as imagined... of the world, and some went to the existentiality of temporal origination, although it is weak, otherwise it would not be included in the world which is what is other than Allah, for the world is the sum of existents, and non-existents are not described as difference terminologically, so they are absolutely not included in the world. His statement: (Rather it resembles being a branch, etc.) He only said 'resembles' because what just passed of their making temporal origination part of the world is not consistent with it; and although this can be interpreted as a concessive proof, their statement of identity in some places also does not suit it; and if by identity is meant only the negation of otherness, it would not apply to what is argued by negating temporal origination, for example. For these reasons he judged it as resemblance and did not definitively state it as branch. His statement: (For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence) i.e., in what is imagined to involve difference, like the argument from the world to the Maker, so it is not objected that this contradicts what that speaker explicitly stated: that the evidence may indicate something by considering its essence, otherwise infinite regress would follow.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on whether the face of indication (وجه الدلالة) must be different from the evidence (الدليل) itself. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical: if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence, then every evidence must have a face of indication that is distinct, leading to infinite regress (التسلسل). The example given is possibility (الإمكان) as a face for the evidence of the world's dependence on a Maker. However, the commentator then critiques this, noting that possibility is a conceptual (اعتباري) matter and that infinite regress only follows if every face is itself an evidence—which can be avoided if one stops at a face that is not evidence. Next, he discusses a second group who say it is not necessary for the face to differ; rather, a thing may indicate by its very essence. He reconciles this with the mashayikh's (المشايخ) principle that an attribute of a thing is neither the thing itself nor entirely other (صفة الشيء لا هو ولا غيره). The commentator explains that this principle does not universally negate difference; some attributes are separable (منفكة) like temporal origination (الحدوث) in the sense of coming from non-existence, while others are inseparable (لازمة) like possibility. The seventh group is introduced, claiming that the face (e.g., huduth) is absolutely other than the evidence (the world). The commentator then shows how the second group's argument, when concessively accepted, actually proves non-difference. The discussion continues with the assertion that there is no third entity between the world and the Maker; everything other than God is the world. This aligns with the mashayikh's view that the face is an attribute of the evidence. A critic (ناقد المحصل) is quoted suggesting that the whole dispute arises from how mutakallimun argue from the existence of contingent things to God, either through possibility or through being preceded by non-existence. Finally, clarification is given that the face of indication being an attribute of the evidence does not conflict with the possibility of indicating by essence, as long as the attribute is not considered separate in that context. The entire passage is a sophisticated logical analysis of the relationship between evidence, face of indication, and infinite regress, emphasizing the flexibility of the mashayikh's principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does the face of indication differ from the evidence based on the mashayikh's principle?
A) Always, because the face is an attribute.
B) Never, because the attribute is neither the same nor different.
C) Only when the attribute is separable from its subject.
D) Only when the attribute is necessary.

Key Takeaway
The face of indication may be identical or different depending on whether the attribute is separable or inseparable, consistent with the mashayikh's principle.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you consider your own faith, are there attributes of your belief that you treat as inseparable (like your conviction in Tawhid) and others as separable (like your level of devotion)? Which ones are you most afraid of losing?
?
The mashayikh's principle helps distinguish between what a thing is and what it is not. In your life, are there aspects of your identity or religion that you mistakenly treat as inseparable from God, when they are actually distinct? How can this lesson refine your understanding of God's attributes?
?
This lesson challenges you to differentiate between essential and accidental attributes. Think of a habit or action you claim is part of your religious character. Is it truly inseparable from your faith, or could it be dropped without harming your iman? Commit to developing one inseparable attribute this week.

Logic and Technical Terms

6 min
The Seventh Group and the Critic's Meta-Analysis
Presents the seventh group's view, concessive argument, and the critic's meta-analysis.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the seventh group's claim that the face of indication is absolutely other than the evidence, and how the critic traces the entire dispute to the method of arguing from contingent existence to God.

Core Idea
The dispute over the face of indication ultimately stems from how we argue from the world to God.

In this final lesson, we examine the seventh group's definitive claim that the face of indication (e.g., temporal origination) is entirely other than the evidence (the world). The commentator then reconciles this with the second group's concessive argument, and a critic provides a meta-level analysis, suggesting that the whole debate arises from the muakallimun's arguments for God's existence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seventh group's claim
Read the passage to find the statement that the face of indication is absolutely other than the evidence.
2
Understand the concessive argument
The second group's statement is reinterpreted as a concessive argument: even if the face is other, the indication may still be through the face itself, leading to non-difference.
3
Learn the critic's origin of the dispute
The critic claims the whole issue arises when mutakallimun argue from contingent existence to God, using either possibility or temporal origination. This shows the practical context.

صفة للدليل منفكة عنه، كالحدوث بمعنى الخروج من العدم إلى الوجود على تقدير وجوده فإنه عن الحادث، كما ستقف عليه في المقصد الثاني من المرصد الرابع في الصفات الوجودية، وقد لا تكون منفكة عنه كالإمكان ، سلم أن الحدوث غير العالم فالاستدلال قد يكون بنفس الحدوث، فحينئذ لا مغايرة بين وجه الدلالة والدليل فلا وجوب وقولهم الحدوث ليس غير العالم إلى استدلال منعي من وجه نعم لو قدم هذا لكان أنسب، فعلى هذا التوجيه ترتبط سوابق الكلام ولواحقه فتأمل. صفة منفكة قوله : (ليس غير العالم مبني على ما أشعر به كلام الفرقة الأولى القائلة بمغايرة الحدوث . واسطة بين العالم الذي هو ما سوی الله تعالى (والصانع) بل كل ما هو مغاير له تعالى فهو داخل فيما سواه، فليس ثمة أمر ثالث هو غير العالم والصانع ونحن نستدل بالعالم على الصانع ( فليس ثمة أمر ثالث هو غير الدليل والمدلول وهذا الذي ذكره هؤلاء ( قريب مما قال مشايخنا : صفة الشيء لا هو ولا غيره كما سيأتي ( بل يشبه أن يكون فرعاً لذلك فإن وجه الدلالة صفة للدليل وستقف عليه) أي على ما ذكره حال الصفة من الموصوف، قال ناقد : المحصل هذه المسألة إنما تجري بین المتكلمين عند استدلالهم بوجود ما سوى الله على وجوده تعالى، فيقولون : لا مشايخنا فيما قوله : (صفة الشيء لا هو ولا غيره) أي بعض الصفات وهي اللازمة على ما سيجيء نقلاً عن الشيخ الأشعري أن الصفات منها ما هو عين الذات كالوجود ومنها ما هو غيره وهي كل صفة أمكن مفارقتها عن الموصوف كصفات الأفعال من كونه خالقاً ورازقاً، ونحوهما ومنها ما يقال : إنه لا عينه ولا غيره وهي ما يمتنع انفكاكه عنه بوجه من الوجوه كالعلم والقدرة، فلا يرد ما يتوهم من أن هذا يقتضي أن يكون قول هؤلاء السلب الكلي مع أنهم مصرحون برفع الإيجاب الكلي . قوله : فإن وجه الدلالة صفة للدليل أي قد يكون صفة الدليل فلا ينافي ما تقدم منه من ( أنه قد يدل الشيء نظرا إلى ذاته وأن الحدوث ليس غير العالم. قوله : (قال) ناقد المحصل هذه المسألة إلخ) لما كان المنشأ الذي ذكره المصنف في غاية البعد نقل منشأ لهذا الاختلاف تقبله الطبائع في الجملة. قوله : ( عند استدلالهم بوجود ما سوى الله على وجوده (تعالى كما يستدلون بالممكنات الموجودة على الواجب ،تعالى كذلك يستدلون بوجود الممكنات على وجود الواجب، إما بإمكانه أو بمسبوقيته بالعدم فالكلام على ظاهره ولا حاجة إلى التأويل على ما وهم ، للعالم، وذهب إليه البعض من وجودية الحدوث وإن كان مزيفاً، وإلا لا يكون داخلاً في العالم الذي هو ما سوى الله تعالى، إذ العالم هو جملة الموجودات وأما المعدومات فلا توصف بالمغايرة اصطلاحاً، فلا تدخل في العالم قطعاً قوله : ( بل يشبه أن يكون فرعاً إلخ ) إنما قال : يشبه لأن ما مر آنفاً من جعلهم الحدوث من جملة العالم لا يلائمه وهذا وإن أمكن حمله على أنه استدلال إلزامي، لكن قولهم بالعينية في بعض المواضع لا يلائمه أيضا ولو أريد بالعينية سلب الغيرية فقط، لم يتجه فيما استدل بنفي الحدوث مثلاً ، ولهذه المعاني حكم بالشبه ولم يقطع بالفرعية . قوله : ( فإن وجه الدلالة صفة للدليل أي فيما يتوهم فيه المغايرة كالاستدلال بالعالم على الصانع ،تعالى فلا يرد أن هذا مخالف لما صرح به ذلك القائل من أن الدليل قد يدل على الشيء نظراً إلى ذاته وإلا لزم التسلسل
The Fifth Observation - The Tenth Objective: Does knowledge of the signified differ. The face of indication being different from the evidence. (But a thing may indicate something else by considering its essence; otherwise) meaning if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence but it is necessary that every evidence has a face of indication that differs from it, then infinite regress would follow. Because we transfer the discussion to that face which is the cause of the evidence's indication, like possibility (al-imkan) for example, for it is also an evidence indicating the existence of the Maker, so it must have a face of indication that differs from it. (And temporal origination (al-huduth)) which is the face of indication is not other than the world which is the evidence. His statement: (It is not necessary, etc.) This and his statement: But a thing may indicate etc. are explicit that these people claimed the removal of obligation. His statement: (For it is also an evidence, etc.) has a discussion because if it is based on possibility being part of the world, then it would be evidence for the existence of the Maker, but it is objected that we do not accept that because it is a conceptual matter; and this indicates that what is evidence for the existence of the Maker must have its face of indication assuming difference as an evidence, and infinite regress only follows if the face of indication of every evidence is an evidence. It is permissible to end at an evidence whose face of indication is not an evidence for anything. And if it is based on the idea that since the evidence is evidence by virtue of that face, the face is in reality an evidence, it is denied because evidence is that through which one can reach correct consideration in it or its states, and consideration does not occur in its face of indication. His statement: (And others said: It is not necessary; rather a thing may indicate, etc.) For if you say: The apparent meaning of these two statements indicates the permissibility of difference in some attributes, and the latter part of the statement from its being based on what the mashayikh said indicates the non-permissibility of difference; I say: Even if the claim of actual basis is granted, we do not accept that it indicates the non-permissibility of difference absolutely. For the mashayikh, may Allah have mercy on them, do not claim for every attribute of a thing that it is neither it nor other. Rather, the attribute according to them may differ from its possessor if it is separable from its possessor, and may not differ if it is concomitant and inseparable, as the commentator will quote from al-Amidi in the sixth objective of the fourth observation on unity, multiplicity, and relation in his statement: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, by convention, and the intended meaning is the necessary attribute. So mere building upon what the mashayikh mentioned and the statement that the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence does not necessitate non-difference, for the face of indication may be an attribute of the evidence separable from it, like temporal origination (al-huduth) meaning coming out of non-existence into existence on the assumption of its existence, for it is something other than the contingent, as you will come to know in the second objective of the fourth observation on existence-based attributes; and it may not be separable from it, like possibility (al-imkan). And know that the seventh group claimed that the face of indication, e.g., temporal origination, is other than the evidence, i.e., the world absolutely. So the statement of the second group who deny obligation, 'Rather a thing may indicate' is an indication of a concessive argument for the negation of obligation, etc., i.e., if it is granted that temporal origination is other than the world, then the indication may be through temporal origination itself, so then there is no difference between the face of indication and the evidence, hence no obligation. And their statement that temporal origination is not other than the world is a prohibitive argument. Yes, if this had been presented earlier it would have been more appropriate. Thus, according to this direction, the preceding and following speech are connected, so ponder. A separable attribute. His statement: (It is not other than the world, based on what the statement of the first group indicates who claim the difference of temporal origination. An intermediary between the world, which is what is other than Allah (and the Maker); rather, everything that is other than Him is included in what is besides Him. So there is no third thing that is other than the world and the Maker, and we argue from the world to the Maker. (So there is no third thing that is other than the evidence and the signified. And this which these people mentioned is close to what our mashayikh said: The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other, as will come; rather it resembles being a branch of that, for the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, and you will come to know it) i.e., the state of the attribute in relation to its possessor. A critic said: al-Muhassal (the summary) of this question only occurs among the mutakallimun when they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, saying: Our mashayikh do not... His statement: (The attribute of a thing is neither it nor other) i.e., some attributes, namely the necessary ones, as will come by way of quote from al-Ash'ari that attributes include what is identical to the essence, like existence; and what is other than it, which is every attribute that can separate from its possessor, like attributes of action: His being Creator, Provider, and the like; and what is said to be neither identical nor other, which is what cannot separate from it in any way, like knowledge and power. So it does not respond to what is imagined that this requires that the statement of these people be absolute negation, while they explicitly state the removal of absolute obligation. His statement: For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence, i.e., it may be an attribute of the evidence, so it does not contradict what preceded from him regarding what he stated that a thing may indicate by considering its essence and that temporal origination is not other than the world. His statement: (A critic said: al-Muhassal of this question, etc.) Since the origin that the author mentioned is extremely remote, he transmitted an origin for this disagreement that natures accept in general. His statement: (When they argue from the existence of what is other than Allah to His existence, as they argue from existing contingent things to the Necessary, similarly they argue from the existence of contingent things to the existence of the Necessary, either by their possibility or by their being preceded by non-existence, so the speech is apparent and there is no need for interpretation, as imagined... of the world, and some went to the existentiality of temporal origination, although it is weak, otherwise it would not be included in the world which is what is other than Allah, for the world is the sum of existents, and non-existents are not described as difference terminologically, so they are absolutely not included in the world. His statement: (Rather it resembles being a branch, etc.) He only said 'resembles' because what just passed of their making temporal origination part of the world is not consistent with it; and although this can be interpreted as a concessive proof, their statement of identity in some places also does not suit it; and if by identity is meant only the negation of otherness, it would not apply to what is argued by negating temporal origination, for example. For these reasons he judged it as resemblance and did not definitively state it as branch. His statement: (For the face of indication is an attribute of the evidence) i.e., in what is imagined to involve difference, like the argument from the world to the Maker, so it is not objected that this contradicts what that speaker explicitly stated: that the evidence may indicate something by considering its essence, otherwise infinite regress would follow.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on whether the face of indication (وجه الدلالة) must be different from the evidence (الدليل) itself. The commentator begins by presenting a hypothetical: if a thing does not indicate something else by its essence, then every evidence must have a face of indication that is distinct, leading to infinite regress (التسلسل). The example given is possibility (الإمكان) as a face for the evidence of the world's dependence on a Maker. However, the commentator then critiques this, noting that possibility is a conceptual (اعتباري) matter and that infinite regress only follows if every face is itself an evidence—which can be avoided if one stops at a face that is not evidence. Next, he discusses a second group who say it is not necessary for the face to differ; rather, a thing may indicate by its very essence. He reconciles this with the mashayikh's (المشايخ) principle that an attribute of a thing is neither the thing itself nor entirely other (صفة الشيء لا هو ولا غيره). The commentator explains that this principle does not universally negate difference; some attributes are separable (منفكة) like temporal origination (الحدوث) in the sense of coming from non-existence, while others are inseparable (لازمة) like possibility. The seventh group is introduced, claiming that the face (e.g., huduth) is absolutely other than the evidence (the world). The commentator then shows how the second group's argument, when concessively accepted, actually proves non-difference. The discussion continues with the assertion that there is no third entity between the world and the Maker; everything other than God is the world. This aligns with the mashayikh's view that the face is an attribute of the evidence. A critic (ناقد المحصل) is quoted suggesting that the whole dispute arises from how mutakallimun argue from the existence of contingent things to God, either through possibility or through being preceded by non-existence. Finally, clarification is given that the face of indication being an attribute of the evidence does not conflict with the possibility of indicating by essence, as long as the attribute is not considered separate in that context. The entire passage is a sophisticated logical analysis of the relationship between evidence, face of indication, and infinite regress, emphasizing the flexibility of the mashayikh's principle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: There is a third entity between the world and God that serves as the face of indication.
Correction: The passage asserts there is no third; everything other than God is the world.

Checkpoint
According to the critic (ناقد المحصل), when does the dispute over whether the face of indication differs from the evidence occur?
A) Only among philosophers
B) When mutakallimun argue from contingent existence to God
C) When discussing the essence of God
D) In debates about the attributes of actions

Key Takeaway
The debate over the face of indication is grounded in the practical method of arguing from the world to God, and the seventh group's absolute difference view is reconciled with other views through conceding the indication itself.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you argue for the existence of God, do you rely on the world's temporal origination or its possibility? Which feels more convincing to your heart—and why? Does the academic debate over the 'face of indication' change the strength of your certainty?
?
The critic says this dispute only arises when we actually argue from contingent existence. Has your own faith ever been shaken by confusion over such technical distinctions? If so, how do you ensure your reasoning remains firm without getting lost in complexities?
?
The mashayikh teach that an attribute is neither identical to nor other than its possessor. Does this principle make you more comfortable with affirming God's attributes, or does it feel like an evasion? Be honest: do you struggle with the idea that we can know God through attributes that are not exactly Him but not separate?

Logic and Technical Terms
intermediate
6 min
The Aspect of Indication as a Conceptual Entity
Debate on whether the aspect of indication is a distinct conceptual entity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the debate over whether the aspect of indication is a conceptual entity distinct from God and creation, and the objection that conceptual distinctions are not externally real.

Core Idea
The aspect of indication is a conceptual tool, not an external existent.

This passage addresses a subtle question in kalam: when we say that the existence of contingent things indicates God’s existence, is the 'aspect of indication' itself a real entity separate from both? The author presents a hypothetical argument, an answer, and then a forceful objection from the theologians. Let’s unpack each layer.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the three moves
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the three distinct parts: a hypothetical claim (يجوز), an answer (وأجاب), and an objection (اعترض).
2
Understand the concept of 'amr iʿtibārī'
The answer describes the aspect as an 'amr iʿtibārī' (conceptual matter), like possibility (imkān) and temporal origination (ḥudūth). Consider what these examples have in common: they are not external objects but mental considerations.
3
Analyze the objection
The theologian objects that 'distinct' (al-mutaghāyirān) in kalam means two externally existing things. Thus, if the aspect is not externally existent, the original argument (that it is not distinct) is correct, making the 'conceptual' answer irrelevant.
Infinite regress (tasalsul) is invoked to show that if it were externally existent, it would lead to an endless chain.
4
Reflect on the dialectic
Consider how this debate hinges on definitions: what does 'distinct' mean? The answer assumes conceptual distinctness, while the objection insists on external distinctness. This reveals underlying assumptions in kalam metaphysics.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يجوز أن يكون وجه دلالة وجود ما سواه على وجوده مغايراً لهما إذا المغاير لوجوده تعالى داخل في وجود ما سواه، والمغاير لوجود ما سواه هو وجوده فقط، وأجاب بأن وجه الدلالة مغاير لوجودهما، وهو أمر اعتباري ليس بموجود في الخارج كالإمكان والحدوث.
قوله : ( داخل في وجود ما سواه إضافة الوجود فيه على نهج قولهم حصول الصورة، وعلى هذا إضافته سابقاً ولاحقاً وإلا فالحدوث على تقدير وجوده داخل لا في وجود ما سوى الله تعالى، بل في نفس ما سواه سبحانه .
قوله : ( وأجاب أن وجه الدلالة (إلخ اعترض عليه بأن المتغايرين عند المتكلمين هما الشيئان الموجودان في الخارج، فالمتكلم إذا استدل بما ذكره على أن وجه الدلالة ليس مغايراً، كان معناه ليس مغايرا موجودا في الخارج، وإلا لزم التسلسل ولا شك في صحة ذلك، فلا معنى للجواب عنه بأنه اعتباري .
It is possible that the aspect of indication of the existence of other than Him upon His existence is different from both, since that which is different from His existence is internal to the existence of other than Him, and that which is different from the existence of other than Him is His existence alone. And he answered that the aspect of indication is different from both of them, and it is a conceptual matter not existing externally, like possibility (al-imkān) and temporal origination (al-ḥudūth).
His statement: (Internal to the existence of other than Him) the attribution of existence in it is in the manner of their saying 'the acquisition of the form,' and on this its attribution is prior and posterior; otherwise, temporal origination, on the assumption of its existence, is internal not to the existence of other than God Almighty, but rather to the essence of other than Him, Exalted is He.
His statement: (And he answered that the aspect of indication (etc.) There was objected to him that 'the two distinct things according to the theologians are the two things existing externally; so if the theologian argues by what he mentioned that the aspect of indication is not different, its meaning is that it is not a different thing existing externally; otherwise an infinite regress would follow, and there is no doubt about the correctness of that. So there is no meaning to the answer about it being conceptual.)
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage discusses whether the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalāla) that leads from the existence of contingent things to the existence of God is distinct from both of them. The first part presents a hypothetical: it could be said that the aspect is distinct, but then that which is distinct from God's existence would be part of the existence of other things, and what is distinct from other things' existence is only God's existence. The answer given is that the aspect is indeed distinct, but it is a conceptual entity (amr iʿtibārī), not an externally existing thing, analogous to possibility (al-imkān) and temporal origination (al-ḥudūth).

Then the commentator (al-Jurjānī) explains a phrase from the original: 'internal to the existence of other than Him'—how existence is attributed in that context. He clarifies that temporal origination, if it existed, would not be internal to the existence of other-than-God but to the essence of that other.

Next, an objection is raised: according to the theologians, 'distinct' means two externally existing things. So when one argues that the aspect is not distinct (i.e., not a separate external entity), it means it does not exist externally; otherwise there would be an infinite regress. Therefore, the answer that it is 'conceptual' is irrelevant because the point is that it is not an external existent, not that it is a mental concept. The passage ends with this objection, leaving it unanswered within this excerpt.

Key Terms
وجه الدلالة
أمر اعتباري
الإمكان
الحدوث
المغاير
التسلسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that 'conceptual' means the aspect does not exist at all, or that it is a mere fiction.
Correction: In kalam, conceptual entities (amr iʿtibārī) exist in the mind and have a kind of reality, though not external existence. They are valid objects of analysis.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the aspect of indication (wajh al-dalāla) is described as:
A) An externally existing entity distinct from both existences
B) A conceptual (iʿtibārī) entity, not externally existent
C) Identical to God's existence
D) Impossible to know

Key Takeaway
The aspect of indication is a conceptual entity, not externally existent, but theologians object that 'distinct' requires external existence, leading to a debate about the nature of conceptual distinctions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that the aspect of indication is a conceptual tool, not an external reality. When you reflect on the signs of God in the world, do you treat them as mere intellectual concepts, or do they lead you to a living awareness of His presence? What would need to change in your daily reflection for these signs to truly impact your heart?
?
The theologians argued that calling something 'distinct' carries specific implications about existence. Are there aspects of your faith that you keep as abstract ideas without letting them shape your actions? Consider your belief in God's oneness (tawḥīd): is it a theoretical concept or a reality that governs your choices? Name one area where you can make this belief more concrete today.
?
In this lesson, even the theologians agreed that the aspect is not externally existent, yet they debated its status. Do you sometimes engage in religious discussions that miss the core purpose—drawing nearer to God? How can you ensure that your study of theology deepens your devotion rather than becoming a mere mental exercise?
